As for the identity of the perpetrators, it is said that it may have been caused by a grudge. The police are currently conducting a secret investigation.

The Ministry of Finance's recent currency reform has stopped the use of coins and stipulated that the banknotes of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications are the legal tender. Other banks with the right to issue banknotes were ordered to stop issuing them as of November 3 of the previous year. However, the Continental Bank took this as a pretext to cancel the contracts it had signed with Huafeng and 12 other banks, totaling 1.75 million yuan, to use the Central Bank's banknotes. The banks unanimously opposed this, arguing that the contracts had not yet expired, and retained lawyer Zhan Jifeng to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court against the Continental Bank and its president, Ye Fuchi, to confirm

The contract is valid and to pay the annual interest on the 40% cash deposit. After the court held a hearing, the Continental Bank also retained lawyer Wang Chuanbi to file a statement of defense. The plaintiff then filed a statement refuting the defendant's arguments point by point. The details have been reported in detail in the newspaper. However, there are many money exchanges in this city that promote famous bank notes, which are so-called "designated banknotes," so this case is considered to have

Serious implications for those who use these notes, and should not be ignored. Therefore, when Judge Huang Dahee continued the trial in the 13th Court at 1:30 PM yesterday, in addition to the representatives of the plaintiff banks, Ma Wenxiang, Liu Ximeng, Yin Huanzhi, and others, more than 40 or 50 people from the financial community attended the hearing. The spectator seats were packed. Judge Huang asked the plaintiff's lawyer about the interest calculation, since the plaintiff requested a judgment on confirming the validity of the contract and paying interest. Lawyer Zhan said that the amount of notes used by each plaintiff

Varies. The interest should be calculated according to the contract based on the amount of security deposited. Please judge that the defendant should pay the full amount from January 1, 24 to the end of the year. The defendant should have no dispute over this fact. The defendant's lawyer Wang Chuanbi then stated that the defendant had not calculated the interest, and the defendant argued that the contract should be terminated. The court then turned to the defendant's lawyer and asked, "The Ministry of Finance has not stopped the circulation of notes that have already been issued."

The defendant's lawyer replied, "The Ministry of Finance's order limited it to November 3 and stated that no more notes could be issued, so the defendant argues that the contract should be terminated." The judge continued to ask, "The point of contention in this case is not the issuance problem. Now, let me ask if the plaintiff has demanded that the defendant continue to issue notes because they have not used up the full amount according to the contract." The lawyer replied, "There is no such situation, and we no longer need to promote sales." The judge asked, "So the notes that have already been sold are still in circulation, and the defendant has not recalled them." The lawyer replied, "That is correct." The judge then raised the issue of the contract signed between the Bank of Communications and the note users,

Which is still valid, and asked the defendant's lawyer about it. The lawyer said that the situations were different and could not be compared. Then lawyer Zhan presented two pages of the notification from the Yanyeh Bank to the note users of the bank regarding interest payments, and stated that the Yanyeh Bank and the Continental Bank are both members of the Four Banks, and their steps should be consistent with regard to note usage. Now that the Yanyeh Bank continues to fulfill the note usage contract and still pays interest according to the contract, why does the Continental Bank want to be different? The defendant's lawyer also

Produced a stack of canceled note usage contracts, saying that the defendant had canceled many contracts with other companies, and they were presented for reference. The plaintiff's lawyer immediately refuted this, saying that some of the canceled contracts had expired, or the term was about to expire, or a special benefit was given before they were canceled, and this could not be used to bind this case. Since Judge Huang believed that the case still needed investigation, he ordered the plaintiff to prepare a detailed interest calculation table and submit it, rescheduling the hearing to the afternoon of February 5 and expressing his hope that the parties would resolve it peacefully outside the court. The lawyers of both parties respected the court's good intentions and withdrew.

Russian Immigrants Concerned: Bakery Homicide Case

The shop owner stabbed his employee to death in a fit of anger; the original sentence was deemed too harsh, leading to an appeal. Bai Liqiang, the 48-year-old Russian owner of a bakery and confectionery shop located at 2346 Avenue D'Ambel in the French Concession, employed a 30-year-old Russian named Sai Miyanuofu. Bai's wife, Bai Qilianzi, informed him that Sai had repeatedly engaged in inappropriate and lewd behavior towards their daughters, Lala and Weiwo Laide, aged nine and five respectively. On the afternoon of November 26th of the previous year, Bai summoned Sai to a small room on the third floor of the shop. He questioned and rebuked Sai, who admitted to the accusations and acted aggressively, which inflamed Bai. Overcome with anger, Bai grabbed a knife

and killed Sai. Afterwards, Bai surrendered himself to the French Concession police. The police department transferred Bai to the Special District Second Court, charging him with homicide under Article 271 of the Criminal Code. After a trial presided over by Judge Zhang Chaozuo, Bai Liqiang was sentenced to twelve years imprisonment on December 7th. Dissatisfied with the heavy sentence, the defendant, Bai, hired attorneys Zhan Jifeng, Zhu Gaorong, and the French lawyer Puleimei, who submitted a petition to the High Court Third Branch, citing reasons for appeal. After the verdict of the Special District Second Court was issued, various Western newspapers in Shanghai

published editorials, arguing that the defendant killed a rogue element in a fit of anger and then surrendered himself. They believed the sentence was too severe and cited Western laws that could exempt the defendant from punishment under such circumstances. Consequently, the French Concession Police Department, in accordance with Article 336, Section 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law, also filed an appeal with the High Court Third Branch for the defendant's benefit, requesting the original verdict be overturned and a lighter sentence imposed. Based on the petition, the High Court Third Branch, led by Acting Chief Judge Sun Honglin, along with Judges Wang Yue and Li Changnian, convened a joint session with Chief Prosecutor Zhao Shibei yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m. to hear the case.

The French Concession Police Department was represented by attorney Fei Xizhen. The attorneys hired by the appellant Bai Liqiang, Zhan, Zhu, and Pu, also arrived on time. This case garnered considerable attention from Westerners in Shanghai, with over a hundred Russian men, women, and children crowding the gallery. All seats were filled, and numerous reporters from various Western newspapers in Shanghai, more than ten in total, attended to observe and record the proceedings. After the court was called to order, the court ordered Bai Liqiang to be brought before the court. His age and occupation were verified, and his testimony was interpreted by translator Zhang Qingchun. After the testimony, the Police Department attorney presented the

reasons for the appeal. Afterwards, the court questioned Bai Liqiang about his reasons for appealing. According to the translated testimony, he was appealing because the original sentence of twelve years was too harsh, and the detailed reasons would be presented by his representatives. The court ordered him to also provide a detailed account, as his representatives were only there to defend him. Bai testified that Sai Miyanuofu had behaved indecently towards his two daughters, which he was initially unaware of. On November 26th, his wife suddenly

called him to stop Sai Miyanuofu. He pressed her for the reason, and she was initially unwilling to say. After repeated questioning, his wife revealed that the older daughter had told her mother that Sai Miyanuofu had been engaging in improper behavior towards the two girls. He summoned Sai to a small room upstairs where flour was stored and questioned him. Sai directly admitted it, saying he was just playing around and that it was no big deal. He was extremely agitated and tried to hit Sai but couldn't find anything to use as a weapon. He saw a sharp knife on a flour sack and used it to strike Sai. Sai immediately rushed at him. He didn't know how

Sai was fatally injured. His mind was confused, he didn't understand, and he didn't know how he surrendered himself to the police. The court then summoned Bai's wife and daughter, along with the Western detective from the police station who handled the case, for detailed and repeated questioning. The process took a considerable amount of time before it was completed. The court then ordered the start of the arguments. The Chief Prosecutor delivered his opinion, followed by arguments between the Police Department attorney and Bai's three attorneys, mainly requesting a lighter sentence or probation. After the arguments were completed, the court announced the end of the arguments and scheduled the verdict for 2 p.m. on the 21st. The appellant, Bai Liqiang, was remanded to custody pending the verdict. By the time the court adjourned, the clock had struck seven.

Land Bureau Reduces Land Transfer Tax

The Land Bureau has been collecting transfer taxes according to the regulations of 8.4% of sales prices, without any increase. After dividing the area for collecting land value tax and changing to collect land value tax, the transfer tax was reduced by 2%. It is now learned that the Land Bureau has separately drafted a method to further reduce the transfer tax, which has been submitted to the Municipal Government by the Finance and Land Bureaus. Upon approval, a public notice will be jointly issued to inform the public. The public notice is extracted below:

According to the regulations, the amount of deed tax to be levied on land sales in the city has been previously stipulated as 6 yuan per 100 yuan of deed price for sales deeds, plus an additional construction special levy of 2 yuan per 100 yuan. For pawn deeds, it is 3 yuan per 100 yuan of deed price, plus an additional construction special levy of 1 yuan per 100 yuan. For those within the land value tax collection area, it is reduced to 2 yuan per 100 yuan, which has been followed. However, it has been found that after private land sales are concluded, they are often concealed from taxation and title transfer. Most landowners inherit the land and pay the grain tax, causing the owner's name to lose its accuracy, which hinders land consolidation. However, the financial capacity of the people has been affected by the sluggish market, making it inevitable that they cannot pay taxes according to regulations. Previously, this bureau drafted a method to reduce taxes for old deeds that have exceeded the time limit for tax payment, which was submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and announced for implementation. Now, although the taxes on old deeds that have exceeded the time limit have been reduced, the current deed tax rate should also be reduced to alleviate the people's financial burden. A method has been drafted and tentatively implemented for one year to observe the effects. It has been submitted to the Municipal Government, which has approved the trial implementation. In addition to amending and reporting the "Provisional Rules for Collecting Real Estate Deed Tax in this City," the method for reducing the transfer tax is attached below. All landowners in the city are hereby notified that in the future, if there is a land transfer, they must comply with the tax payment and not betray the intent of sympathy and tax reduction. This special announcement is made, as follows: Method for reducing land transfer tax: For land located in plots where permanent leases can be established and which have obtained land practice certificates, a 1% transfer tax will be levied upon sale and transfer. For land that has not been announced for certificate exchange, the transfer tax will be changed to 4% uniformly. For land holding land practice certificates and not conforming to the first item, if the land is located within the area for collecting provisional land value tax, the transfer tax will be changed to 1%. If the land is not located within the land value tax collection area, the transfer tax will be changed to 4%. For land located in areas where land practice certificates have not yet been developed and not conforming to the first item, a 4% transfer tax will be levied. January, 25th year of the Republic of China. Cai Zengji, Director of the Finance Bureau and concurrently Acting Director of the Land Bureau.

Ministry of Finance Approves Stamp Tax Method for Rent Books

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce issued a notice yesterday stating: "To whom it may concern, regarding the matter of how to affix stamps to the rent book issued by the Public Security Bureau, this association has repeatedly telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for approval. Now, we have received approval No. Shui Zi 8353 stating that the first page of the rent book submitted by the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau contains the lease agreement. If the tenant fills in the location and rent of the rented house in this agreement and signs or affixes a seal, regardless of whether there is another lease, it has already taken effect and the tenant who made the lease should affix a two-cent stamp according to law. The rent receipts attached to the rent book must be issued to the tenant one by one and are of the nature of money receipts, so the landlord should affix a stamp according to law each time this receipt is issued. However, in ordinary rent books, although there is a lease on the first page, the monthly rent is collected based on this rent book and no separate rent receipt is given. Therefore, this rent book is a certificate with more than two natures. According to Article 8 of the Stamp Tax Law, if the same certificate has more than two natures and the tax rates are different, the higher tax rate should be applied. The landlord should affix stamps according to the regulations in item 4 of the tax rate table for account books, and the tenant does not need to affix any more stamps on the first page. Please be informed, etc." With this, the corresponding letter is sent for your information and compliance.

Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau Establishes Overseas Chinese Inquiry Office

Handling guidance, answering questions, and consulting matters. The Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau has consulted with customs authorities several times last year, intending to set up an Overseas Chinese Inquiry Office inside the Jianghai Customs Wharf to handle guidance of overseas Chinese work and answer inquiries from returning overseas Chinese. Its intention was excellent, but it could not be realized because there was no space available in the customs house to set up the inquiry office. According to Mr. Jian Jinglun, the director of the bureau, the bureau realized that overseas Chinese have been away from their homeland for a long time, and once they return, they often have little knowledge of the situation in their motherland. Moreover, Shanghai is a place where people from all over the world gather, and the situation is complicated, so there are possibilities for being cheated. Therefore, at the beginning of the bureau's establishment, it contacted the customs authorities repeatedly, requesting permission to set up an Overseas Chinese Inquiry Office in the customs house to prepare for inquiries from overseas Chinese and to send personnel to be stationed there on a regular basis to provide guidance. However, due to location constraints, it was impossible to cede land, and the establishment had to be temporarily suspended. Now, observing the situation from all sides, it seems that there is no room for further delay, so it is proposed to attach the inquiry office to the bureau first, and then expand the organization after a suitable location is found, so that overseas Chinese returning to the country will know where to inquire.

Zhegan Railway Opens Today

The image shows the Guixi Bridge of the Zhegan Railway, photographed during a test run on the 9th of this month. The bridge is over 1,300 feet long, divided into thirteen spans, each spanning 100 feet, with a total construction cost of 800,000 yuan. It was contracted by Mr. Tao Guilin of the Fuyiji Construction Factory, a famous architect in Shanghai. The engineers responsible for supervision were Peng Qi, Cui Erfeng, and Zhou Yuhong. Construction began in November of the 23rd year of the Republic of China and was completed in December of the 24th year of the Republic of China. The project suffered repeated floods, resulting in unrecoverable losses, and in June of the 24th year, it suffered the worst flood in sixty years, resulting in significant losses. The difficulties of inconvenient transportation, difficult transportation, and rapid water flow made construction difficult. It is said that the actual work on the bridge took less than six months to complete, which can be described as swift. During the test run on the 9th, nineteen trailers were used, and the results were very satisfactory. The entire railway will hold an opening ceremony in Nanchang today.

Seafarer Groups; National Salvation United Association Ceases Activities

The China Seafarer Groups National Salvation United Association was originally organized by seven seafarer groups, including the China Marine Engineers United Association, the China Merchant Marine Officers Association, the Navigation Magazine, the China Wireless Telegraphers Welfare Association, the Beijun'an Association, and the China Merchants Bureau Jun'an Association. It was intended to engage in national salvation work, hoping to save the country from danger and seek the survival of seafarers. It is now reported that the association was summoned yesterday by the Special Party Headquarters of the China Seafarers for a discussion. Grand Hotel Homicide Case: Court Opens Trial

Defendants Five Ordered to Provide Solid Shop Guarantees

On December 31st of last year, Wang Lu and other workers from a certain newspaper rented Room 332 at the Grand Hotel on East Xinqiao Road to celebrate the New Year holiday. Unexpectedly, around 1:00 AM, two women suddenly appeared, claiming to be looking for someone named Zhang. Wang replied that there was no Zhang there. The two women immediately left, but within minutes, they returned with more than ten hooligans, all dressed in blue short shirts and trousers. They forcibly accused Wang and Lu of being lewd, and without asking questions, they attacked, injuring Wang's head. Lu's left eye was also punched and swollen. It was said that the internal injuries were very serious. The hotel tea boy, hearing the noise, rushed to mediate but was also beaten. Seeing their objective achieved, the thugs fled in all directions. The tea boy, Yang Jusheng, only managed to apprehend Zhao Wenjun, Wang Aliu, Zhang Genfa, Jiang Asan, and Shen Changsheng. He reported to the police, who charged them with assault and battery in the Second Special District Court. The trial opened yesterday morning at 9:00 AM in the court's eighth criminal division, presided over by Judge Sun Pengxian. First, the first plaintiff, Wang, testified that he was beaten and injured and that he did not know the defendants. He believed that they were incited by someone behind the scenes and requested an investigation. Later, the hotel tea boy stated that the defendants originally wanted to rent Room 306 (next door to Room 332), but because they looked like hooligans, the tea boy refused. As a result, they rented Room 326 at the south of the Grand Hotel. This clearly shows that the incident was premeditated. The second plaintiff, Lu, hired lawyer Yao Junyu to represent him. Yao stated that Lu was unable to attend court due to his injuries. When questioned, the defendants Zhao Wenjun, Wang Aliu, Zhang Genfa, Jiang Asan, and Shen Changsheng gave evasive answers. Lawyer Yao Junyu requested severe punishment. Judge Sun Pengxian ordered the five defendants, Zhao Wenjun, to provide solid shop guarantees. They were detained without bail, and the hearing was adjourned for two weeks.

Teasing Women Leads to Death by Falling

Zhang Daowen, a man from Yangzhou in his late thirties, went to 107 Laowende Lane at the intersection of Pingliang Road and Ningguo Road in East Shanghai yesterday. Zhang worked at the Tongxing Cotton Mill at the intersection of Guangxin Road in Yangshupu. Although Zhang was in his forties, he was naturally frivolous. He would tease any woman who passed his door, and the neighbors knew of his bad nature but did not bother to argue with him. Yesterday afternoon, around 2:00 PM, Zhang was working on the second floor of the Tongxing Mill when he suddenly caught sight of a young woman walking below. Zhang's heart was stirred, and he thought it was an opportunity not to be missed. He rushed to the window, leaned out, and began to tease the woman. While he was excitedly enjoying himself, he lost his balance and fell headfirst from the window, his head hitting the ground, and his brains splattering. By the time the mill's staff arrived, Zhang was already dying. He was immediately taken to the hospital by car but died soon after. His body was then sent to the morgue to await a court examination.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The 265th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Exchange Certificates states: In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this council is responsible for inspecting the number of exchange certificates issued by this bank and its reserves. The 265th inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on January 11, 1936. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) Total amount of exchange certificates issued: 184,866,250 silver dollars, including 166,435,520 silver dollar certificates and 18,430,730 subsidiary currency certificates. Total amount of exchange certificate reserves: 184,866,250 silver dollars, including 123,165,050 silver dollars in cash reserves. These cash reserves include 68,162,382.6 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuing branches and sub-branches, and 55,002,667.4 silver dollars deposited with other banks. Guarantee reserves totaled 61,700,200 silver dollars. (B) Total amount of customs gold exchange certificates issued: 373,324.7 customs gold units. Total amount of customs gold exchange certificate reserves: 373,324.7 customs gold units. These reserves included 7,351.95 taels of standard gold, valued at 50779, totaling 373,324.7 customs gold units. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the remainder must be guaranteed by legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the current reserve exceeds 60%, and the guaranteed reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. January 14, 1936, Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank; Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilu.

Shanghai French Municipal Council Account Closure Notice

The Shanghai French Municipal Council issued a notice yesterday regarding the closure of the accounts for the year 1935. In order to facilitate the closure of the 1935 accounts, the Council hereby notifies all bidders that all unpaid bills for 1935 must be submitted to the Council's Finance Department before February 1 of this year. If this deadline is missed, the funds will not be received until 1937. Please pay attention to this and do not delay. This notice is issued by Pei Dihuan, Acting General Manager.

Shanghai's Seasoning Powder Industry: Editor of China Credit Letter

(Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce, Part 9)

I. Origin

Seasoning powder is a newly emerging chemical product that has only recently been added to the human diet. This is because after the German scientist Liedharson invented the extraction of sodium glutamate from grains, Dr. Ikeda of Japan discovered that it could be used to make seasoning powder. The method of manufacturing this powder is to first extract gluten from flour, combine it with hydrochloric acid, alcohol, and other substances, and then grind it into powder to become seasoning powder. The oldest brand of seasoning powder made by the Japanese is "Aji-no-moto," which has been sold on the market for a long time. According to estimates by people in the industry, the promotion of "Aji-no-moto" in our country was managed by the Japanese company Suzuki & Co. In the past, when imports were at their peak, they averaged 200,000 yuan per month. This shows the increasing standard of living of the Chinese people and the urgent need for seasoning powder. Therefore, patriotic people rose up to imitate it themselves to save this drainage. The Geng Taihe Seasoning Powder Factory, established in Shanghai in 1922, was the beginning. Afterward, many others followed suit, such as the Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate Factory, established in 1923, and the Tianyi Monosodium Glutamate Factory, opened in 1926. From 1929 to 1931, five factories, including Hongfu and Taiyi, sprang up, which was a great boom. Later, due to the Shanghai Incident, the world economic panic, and the return of Japanese goods, the industry declined. Only the Tianyuan Monosodium Glutamate Factory was newly established, and closures were common, such as the Weizhong and Gengtai factories, which were relatively large. As of today, only six companies in Shanghai have a relatively large production scale: Tianchu, Tianyi, the Seasoning Department of China Chemical Industry Society, Taiyi, Tiansheng, and Tianyuan.

As mentioned earlier, seasoning powder was invented by the Japanese and has been sold in our market for a decade. However, after Chinese factories began producing seasoning powder, the number of domestic seasoning powders increased, and Japanese goods were squeezed out to a considerable extent. After the "September 18th Incident" in Shenyang, the Chinese people unanimously boycotted Japanese goods, and Japanese seasoning powder almost disappeared. This was truly a blessing for national industry. However, in the past two years, the situation between China and Japan has changed drastically again, and the government and the public are competing to advocate friendship, so Japanese goods are selling unimpeded again. Currently, the yellow-tin and white-tin seasoning powders sold in various Nanhua stores on the market are all imported Japanese goods. These tin seasoning powders have no labels or trademarks, and are easily mixed and sold on the market. Some unscrupulous merchants are willing to repackage them and pretend they are domestic goods, which makes the situation even worse. It is estimated that the current annual imports average about one million yuan, so we should pay attention to its development prospects.

II. Current Situation of Major Chinese Factories: Of the seasoning powder factories currently existing in this city, only six companies, including Tianchu, are relatively large, as mentioned earlier. Their current situation is described below:

1. Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate Factory: The factory was established in 1923 with an initial capital of only 50,000 yuan. It was established by wealthy merchants Zhang Yiyun, Wu Yun Chu, Wang Dongyuan, and others in partnership. It currently has three factories, all located on Caishi Road and Xinqiao Road in the French Concession. The distribution office was previously located in Zhongwang Lane on Ningbo Road and has now been moved to near Zilai Street on Route Edouard. The factory is equipped with steam boilers, flour kneading machines, Shanghai machines, centrifugal machines, and other equipment. The first factory is used for cutting and manufacturing, and has 150 to 160 workers. The second factory occupies a large area and was previously used for bottling and decorating, and has more than 200 workers. The third factory is used for white-making and has more than 100 workers. It is said that the expenses of each factory are about 10,000 yuan per month. The factory's "Buddha Hand" brand monosodium glutamate is white and delicious, comparable to the Japanese "Aji-no-moto." The company also produced a second brand called "Guding" a few years ago to compete with its competitors in the same industry. The monthly production is about 20,000 pounds. The turnover was only tens of thousands of yuan at first, but after 1926, it increased dramatically. In recent years, it has reached about 2 million yuan per year, generating a great deal of profit. Last autumn, the factory had plans to reorganize into a limited company. This autumn, the reorganization was successful, and the capital was increased to 2 million yuan, most of which was transferred from accumulated public funds over the years. It is said that only a small number of new shareholders were recruited.

2. Tianyi Monosodium Glutamate Factory: The factory was established in July 1926. Initially, its scope was very small. It was opened in partnership by Ye Mojun, Shui Weichen, and others with a capital of only 10,000 yuan. Due to the expansion of the scope, the capital was increased to 50,000 yuan the following year. With hard work, there has been progress every year. It has now been reorganized into a limited company, and the capital has also been increased to 200,000 yuan. The factory has two manufacturing plants, one on Huade Road and one on Kunming Road. The distribution office is located at 243 Zhifu Road, and a branch distribution office is located on Johnston Road in Hong Kong. Its application machinery is considered complete, and there are often more than 100 workers. Its "Lotus" brand monosodium glutamate is quite popular. A second brand, "Golden Star" seasoning powder, was also produced a few years ago, and its quality is also good. It is said that the annual turnover is often around 1 million yuan.

3. The Seasoning Department of the China Chemical Industry Society: The society has a wide scope and a capital of 1 million yuan. Seasoning is only one of its businesses, named "Guanyin Powder." It also uses by-products to manufacture soy sauce essence. The equipment in the factory, such as starch machines, saccharifiers, and carbonizers, is very complete. The annual turnover is 400,000 to 500,000 yuan. Recently, it has also launched a second brand, "Wei Sheng," to meet market sales.

4. Taiyi Malt Extract Powder Factory: The factory was established in August 1929 with a capital of 30,000 yuan. It was opened in partnership by Wang Zhenyu, Zhang Jingchu, and others. It originally had two factories, the first at 85 Haichang Branch Road in Zhabei, and the second at 55 Hengqing Lane on Beile Road in the French Concession. Unfortunately, the second factory was completely destroyed by a boiler explosion in August 1934 (more than 30 workers died, and the factory owner Zhang Jingchu also died in the accident), so only one factory remains. The factory is not large, and the equipment is relatively simple. Its "Double Peach" brand malt extract powder is also sold at a lower price and is still welcomed by ordinary people.

Western YMCA Basketball: Pirates Retain Championship

Xie Xing Loses by Four Points

Result: 45 to 49

The Xie Xing basketball team repeated Ji Fu's mistake again, failing to score baskets, losing to the Pirates by a score of 45 to 49. If they could have made every penalty shot, they really could have won. The Pirates have now secured the championship with eight wins in eight games. Even if they lose to Donghua in the last game, it will not have any impact. The standings for Group A are listed below, so you can see the situation at a glance:

Taking the Lead First The match was delayed until 9:05 PM to begin. After the jump ball, Pirate Pissell, assisted by Carson, scored first. Xie Xing responded calmly. Qiu Guangxie scored first, and Weng Ren'an attacked second, quickly taking the lead with a score of 4 to 2. Ryan then tied the score. Xu Heng made a long shot, and Zhou Dayun succeeded with a free throw, and Xie Xing took the lead again with a score of 7 to 6. Afterward, Weng Ren'an and Xu Heng added five more points, and the Pirates fell behind with a score of 6 to 12.

Pirates Overcome After this, the Pirates gradually found success. Smith made two free throws, and Ryan scored under the basket, tying the score at 12. Squia committed a foul, and Zhang Jinxiang threw the ball too low, losing the opportunity to gain the upper hand. Carson scored with a shot and a free throw, and took the lead with a score of 15 to 12.

Following the Trend Zhang Jinxiang made a long shot, and the score was only one point behind. The Pirates then took advantage of the jump ball advantage of center Ryan. Smith scored three times in a row, and Squia put the ball in with one hand, and the score became 25 to 14. Zhang Jinxiang did not give up, and scored again. Ryan also returned the favor in the same way. Finally, Zhang Jinxiang showed his ability, and the first half ended with a score of 25 to 18.

Xie Xing Takes the Lead Xie Xing became more courageous in the second half. Zhou Dayun first made the score 20 to 15. Carson was quick with his attacks, and Xu Heng committed a foul, resulting in one point on the free throw. Zhang Jinxiang then scored two more shots, and the score became 24 to 26, only two points behind. The Pirates continued their efforts, and Carson, Smith, and Ryan all came at the right time, and scored four goals in a row. Then the score became 40 to 31. Zhou Dayun added four points, and Zhang Jinxiang was very brave, chasing the score to 39 to 42. Pirate White entered the field, replacing Pissell. Xie Xing's Zhou Dayun committed four fouls and was removed from the field, and Shen Chongjiao replaced him. Xu Heng and Shen Chongjiao made two shots, and Xie Xing took the lead with a score of 43 to 42.

The Key to Victory It is a pity that they could not maintain this lead. The Pirates were very active. Carson, Smith, and White scored one after another, and the score became 48 to 43. Xie Xing's Qiu Guangxie jumped up from the crowd and threw the ball in, making the score 45 to 48. Finally, Carson made a free throw, resulting in the exciting score of 49 to 45. Xie Xing lost by four points.

Evaluation of Skills The performance of the entire Xie Xing team was no worse than that of the Pirates. Zhang Jinxiang, Weng Ren'an, and others could attack and defend, and were truly rare talents. It is a pity that the entire team was not accurate with their shots, which led to their loss. However, in terms of their tireless struggle, they were glorious even in defeat. Pirate Ryan was tall and strong, which gave him an advantage. Carson was intelligent and courageous, and made all nine free throws, making him the only hero of the Pirates.

China Youth Basketball Kicks Off Yesterday: Qingzhong and Two Other Teams Win

Bank Group: Shanghai Jia Overcomes Zhongnan Team

School and Business Group Matches Become One-Sided

The 7th Men's and Women's Basketball League organized by China Youth kicked off at 5:00 PM yesterday at the association's gymnasium. The opening match was Qingzhong vs. Gezhi in the school group. Qingzhong has strong strength, and Gezhi was not their opponent, suffering a crushing defeat with a score of 51 to 15. This was followed by Shanghai Jia vs. Zhongnan in the bank group. Shanghai Jia has talent in every age group. Although Zhongnan has one or two strong players, they were still no match. The match became one-sided, with a score of 62 to 37. The third game was Guangyi Jia vs. Xiangtai Yi. The strength of the two sides was very different, and the match was not exciting. Guangyi Jia triumphed with a score of 56 to 9. The details of yesterday's match are as follows:

Qingzhong Defeats Gezhi: In the opening match, Qingzhong vs. Gezhi, Qingzhong has young players such as Yan Juxian, and their strength is still stable. Gezhi ultimately surrendered. In the first half, Hu Shouchang and Liu Mingda of Qingzhong made every shot, but fortunately, Gezhi's defense was quite tight, and the score difference was not far, 22 to 11, with Qingzhong in the lead. Not long after the start of the second half, Gezhi's main players He Shuhu and Feng Yaosen were successively called out for four fouls, and their strength became more unstable. It seemed as if it was entirely Qingzhong's world. Yang Mingda showed off his skills under the basket, and the score soared, like a whirlwind sweeping away the clouds. Later, Gezhi was exhausted, but their spirit remained consistent. In the end, Qingzhong defeated Gezhi with a score of 51 to 15.

Shanghai Defeats Zhongnan: Next was Shanghai Jia vs. Zhongnan, the first match in the bank group. Shanghai has many talents, such as Ren Jiexing and Ye Zuyun, and their strength is tough. Zhongnan also has Zhao Qingxiang and Lin Yunchao, who are not weak. The match was quite exciting. Shanghai opened the scoring. Ren and Ye combined well, and the score increased rapidly. Lin Yunchao and Zhao Qingxiang of Zhongnan also scored successively, and the score was very close. However, Zhongnan's shooting was inaccurate, which was a big disadvantage. Shanghai's momentum was strong, and Ren and Li scored consecutively. In the first half, Shanghai took the lead with a score of 35 to 14. In the second half, Zhongnan was careful and tried to recover, but Shanghai's defense was very tight, with no chance to take advantage of. In the end, Shanghai defeated them with a score of 62 to 37.

Guangyi Defeats Xiangtai: Guangyi is a rising force with many strong players. Xiangtai's strength is ordinary, and they were not their opponent. In the first half, Xiangtai worked hard, and the game was lively. Guangyi's Wen and Liu did not fully exert themselves, only taking the lead with a score of 19 to 7. In the second half, Guangyi brought in Lu Chongrui, and their momentum began to rise. Xiangtai was already exhausted. Guangyi's score increased sharply, and Xiangtai's defense became more lax. Lu Chongrui was unstoppable, shooting from long range. At this point, Xiangtai could only parry and could not fight back. In the end, they lost to Guangyi with a score of 56 to 9. The results of yesterday's match are recorded below: School Group: Qingzhong defeated Gezhi, 51 to 15; Bank Group: Shanghai Jia defeated Zhongnan, 62 to 37; Business Group: Guangyi Jia defeated Xiangtai Yi, 56 to 9.

Educational News

Results of the Guangdong Provincial Examination Announced

(Jinan, 14th Dispatch) In the winter provincial examination for middle school and normal school students in this province, 22 schools and 1,472 people participated. 461 people passed the entire examination.

Hubei Province Holds Graduation Examination

The Province is Divided into Eleven Districts

(Hankou Correspondence) The graduation examination for middle school and normal school students in Hubei Province was originally scheduled to be held on the 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of this month. Due to students participating in the national salvation movement, the school authorities advanced the vacation, almost stopping the examination. Now that the student movement has come to an end, the students have requested the education department to hold the examination as usual. However, the period is too short. The outer districts will start the examination on the 12th, and the Wuhan districts will start on the 13th. The entire province is divided into eleven districts and will be completed by the 15th. The results will be announced within two weeks.

Guangdong Province Subsidizes

Impoverished Counties to Run Free Education

(Changsha, 14th Dispatch) The provincial government has appointed Huang Shiheng as the president of Hunan University, to take office on February 1st. In order to implement a three-year administrative plan, Guangdong Province has allocated funds from the provincial treasury to subsidize impoverished counties to promote compulsory education. The amount of funds allocated and the methods of establishing schools in the 23rd year for the designated subsidized counties, including Ganen, Changjiang, Lingshui, Lehui, Fangcheng, Lingshan, Xuwen, Fengchuan, Kaijian, Yangshan, Ruyuan, Wengyuan, Xinfeng, Lianping, Heping, Fengshun, Nanao, Fogang, and Baoan, will continue to be handled in accordance with the original regulations. From the 24th year onwards, the provincial treasury subsidy funds will be designated for opening short-term primary schools. The counties subsidized for opening short-term primary schools, in addition to the above-mentioned 20 counties including Ganen, will continue to add short-term primary schools, and 20 counties including Dan County will be newly added subsidized short-term primary schools. All recipients of subsidized funds must open new short-term primary schools and must not reorganize existing schools. Each school should be based on opening one class in principle, with 40 students per class. When necessary, two classes may be combined into one school. Each school is limited to accepting out-of-school children aged 9 to 16. The length of study is set at one year. Each school will be selected by an education official to serve as both principal and teacher. If two classes are combined into one school, one principal and teacher will be selected, and one teacher will be selected. The candidates for principals and teachers of each school are: graduates of the provincial primary school teacher training institute, graduates of provincial normal schools, and graduates of county and municipal normal schools. Their treatment is as follows: the principal and teacher's monthly salary is 35 yuan, and the teacher's monthly salary is 30 yuan. Each school's start-up fee is 120 yuan, and the annual public fee is 60 yuan (5 yuan per month), which is the responsibility of the county government to raise. The subjects of short-term primary schools are civic training, national language (dictation, composition, writing), arithmetic, common sense, and physical education. The teaching time of each school is set at eight sessions per day, with each session lasting 30 minutes.

Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Examines and Recruits Overseas Students to Study in the UK

Number of Places Decided: 21

Divided into 15 Subjects Including English

The Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund Board of Trustees is recruiting 21 fourth-term overseas students to study in the UK. The results were reported yesterday. It is learned that the distribution of their academic fields is as follows: English, one place (graduates from all departments of literature and linguistics are eligible to apply); Western History, one place (focusing on modern history and international relations); Law, two places (one focusing on civil law and one focusing on administrative law); Economics, two places (one focusing on industrial economics and one focusing on private economics); Mathematics, two places (focusing on applied mathematics); Physics, two places (focusing on applied physics); Geophysics, one place (graduates from all departments of geology, geography, mathematics, and physics are eligible to apply); Chemistry, one place (focusing on physical chemistry); Geography, three places (focusing on natural geography); Biology, one place (focusing on animal physiology); Mechanical Engineering, one place (focusing on locomotive manufacturing); Civil Engineering, one place (focusing on bridge engineering); Aeronautical Engineering, one place; Shipbuilding Engineering, one place; Theoretical Medicine, two places (focusing on anatomy or bacteriology).

The Fourth Annual Meeting of the Chinese Social Education Society: The Third Batch of Shanghai Members Left for Guangdong Yesterday

Sun Yat-sen University Subsidizes the Society's Domestic Travel Expenses

He Tianjian's Landscape Masterpieces to be Published

Mr. He Tianjian of Wuxi, also known as a strong man on the top of the Hundred-Foot Building, is one of the leading painters of modern times. His landscapes deeply understand the mysteries of the Northern Song Dynasty. In recent years, he has lived in Shanghai and worked hard on the art movement. In addition to serving as the executive director of the Chinese Painting Association, he has also spared no effort to sponsor the National Painting Monthly, which is popular throughout the country. Since he visited the famous mountains and rivers of Zhejiang at the invitation of the Zhejiang Construction Department last year, his style has changed greatly, and he has created many unique styles. A part of the works has been published in Southeastern Scenery and National Painting Monthly. It is now heard that Mr. He will use collotype to print 17 of his most recent masterpieces. They can be published soon. The printing and style are extremely exquisite, and the price is only three yuan. It is heard that Mr. He, in order to widely disseminate them, will offer a 50% discount to those who directly pre-order them before February 1st at No. 17, Xihu Fang, Ximen Road, French Concession, Shanghai.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (1) (5) (2) Louisa M.

— Original by Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

When Ned said it, his expression was so depressed that Don could no longer bear it, so he muttered to himself in a broken voice, "You won't have to wait long." After saying that, he walked away quickly and was not seen for several hours.

Since there was such an unfortunate mess this week, everyone was suspicious and bored, so the days felt particularly long. When the children saw that Don was a little different on Sunday, they asked each other, "What's wrong with Don?" Usually he was happy and angry, but that day he was very silent, and no one could pry into his heart. When they were walking, he left the crowd and walked alone, returning later than others. He didn't participate in the evening conversation, but sat alone in the shadows, busy with his own thoughts, as if he didn't hear anything. Later, Mrs. Shu took out the cultivation book and showed him a particularly good report card. Although he looked at it, he didn't smile at all, and only said:

"Do you think I can still pass?"

"Very good, very good, Don! I'm so happy, because I often think you just need a little help to make you a good kid." Topic: The Reasons for Rural Decline. Speaker: Zou Shuwen. Time: 6:30 PM to 7:00 PM. Frequency: 660 (Central Broadcasting Station)

--This Month's Gold Short Still Less Than One Yuan--

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange experienced a sharp drop in the market, followed by a sudden rebound, as the reporter expected. Market rumors have not subsided, and arbitrage trading has not taken action. In the absence of profitable conditions, it is naturally impossible to swap. It is also reported that some have already prepared to deliver and are unwilling to swap. The current situation is not optimistic. Yesterday, numbers 4 and 69 were buying in large quantities, and retail investors were also covering their short positions. This kind of return wind is a due phenomenon, but the trend is likely to be unsustainable. A sharp rise and quick retreat will inevitably result in the short side prevailing again. Judging from the sales of numbers 48 and 34.43, as well as the Beibang, and the short covering by the long side, the pressure is still heavy and it is not yet the time to expand. Spring and Autumn

New Year in Huizhou

— (Fang Zheng)

In my hometown of Huizhou, there is a New Year custom called "Going Out." On New Year's morning, the entire family, one by one, lines up to go out. The eldest leads the team, and each person carries a paper lantern. They walk slowly for several dozen steps, then stop to burn incense and pray. From the eldest to the youngest, they bow and then light firecrackers, the so-called "Three Consecutive Launches." This custom is very common; almost every family in my hometown practices this tradition. There is also a custom called "Opening the Brush," which seems more refined and is limited to those who study or do business. "Opening the Brush" involves writing auspicious phrases such as "Opening the Brush on New Year's Day brings good fortune to all things" or "Trying the Brush on New Year's Day brings good luck to all matters." After writing, the phrases are pasted near the writing desk or displayed in the living room. There is also a custom called "Sending Yuan Shi," which involves visiting relatives or friends on the second day of the New Year. Everyone exchanges "Yuan Shi," but not the real Yuan Shi, but large cakes made of flour. They are made by southern goods stores in the style of Shanghai steamed buns, hollow inside, with words like "Blessings and Wealth" or "Small Investment, Big Returns" written on them. When giving the cakes, people say, "I'm giving you a pair of Yuan Shi, eat them and make Yuan Shi," to bring wealth. The superstitions of the people can be seen in this.

Seven-Family Tea and Hundred-Family Lock

— Zhou Xian

"Seven-Family Tea" and "Hundred-Family Lock" are very popular superstitious customs in my hometown, Suzhou.

Seven-family tea is said to cure all kinds of stomach problems. For example, chest discomfort and indigestion can be cured by drinking seven-family tea. Seven-family tea is made by begging for a pinch of tea leaves from each of seven different Zheng families across the street. Those who drink seven-family tea are mostly poor people. When they get sick, they can't afford to see a doctor, especially for minor illnesses. Of course, they can't afford to spend money on medicine, so they beg for seven-family tea to help them. I have never drunk seven-family tea, so I don't know if it is effective. I also don't know if tea leaves can cure diseases. In any case, the tea leaves from the seven families may have been bought from the same tea shop or even picked from the same tea tree. So, I advise those who believe in seven-family tea to just save themselves the trouble and brew tea from their own tea canisters.

Hundred-family locks are for wealthy and poor families who have children and are afraid that they will be sick. So, they prepare one hundred red paper envelopes and ask relatives and friends for a copper coin. When each of the one hundred red paper envelopes contains a copper coin, they pour them out and have a goldsmith make a gold lock. Although a gold lock costs at least ten or more yuan, the one hundred coins that were begged must be given to the goldsmith as payment. It is said that wearing this hundred-family lock will ensure a long life. Every time I go back to my hometown, people ask me for money. Once, I said to a certain Mrs. who asked me for a coin, "I heard that wearing a hundred-family lock is very dangerous because if something happens to the children in the hundred families, the child wearing the hundred-family lock will also be affected." When the lady heard me say this, her face turned pale, and she stopped.

This ridiculous method of defeating the hundred-family lock is actually using superstition to resist superstition, which is not worthy of emulation. However, at a time when education is not widespread and the people's intelligence is not highly developed, I think that if you are unwilling to spend a single coin in reality, but on the surface, you want to put up the banner of breaking superstition, this kind of ridiculous propaganda can be very useful.

New Year in England

— Yu Translation

The English have several customs related to saying goodbye to the old year and welcoming the new year that resemble superstitions. People living north of Twit consider New Year's Eve more important than New Year's Day. People living in Scotland must hold a "Hogmanay" family banquet on New Year's Eve. The banquet should begin after the new year has started, at least after the midnight bells have rung, so that they can drink to their hearts' content. The origin of this custom is probably to express the joy of passing the old year and the ease of entering the new year. Scots living overseas still maintain this custom.

If the fire suddenly goes out during the Hogmanay family banquet, it is a very bad omen. If a neighbor comes to borrow fire during the banquet, the host will not give it to him under any circumstances; otherwise, all the good luck of the year will be given away. In some places, people believe that the person who pours the last glass of wine from the last bottle during the New Year's Eve dinner is extremely lucky and is called "the lucky glass of wine," but it must happen by chance and cannot be arranged in advance. If this lucky glass of wine is drunk by an unmarried person, then it is predicted that they will have good fortune and will get married in the coming year.

If you have nothing in your pockets on New Year's morning, then you will live a year of poverty. People with empty hands cannot enter other people's homes on New Year's Day. The first guest to offer New Year's greetings is called the First Foot, and the English take this very seriously. If the first person to cross the threshold is a woman, then it is certain that the year's luck will not be good. In Klock Pashar, a black-haired person is considered a lucky First Foot, and the most unlucky person is a red-haired person. In some places, people prepare a cup of wine and a piece of cake to offer to the First Foot.

In Sussex, groups of young men and women gather in groups of three or five and go to people's homes to be the First Foot. The first person gets a silver coin, a piece of chopped cake, and a cup of hot elderberry wine with sugar and spices. The second person gets a copper coin. There is also a custom here that you must not take anything out of the house on New Year's Day, but it doesn't matter if you bring things into the house. Even the smallest and cheapest things, such as tea leaves, potato peels, and coal ash, should be carefully kept overnight and taken out the next morning. This will ensure that income exceeds expenses throughout the year.

Little West Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 23: Raising High Arguments Around the Room to Start a Lawsuit; Forgetting Grudges by Pouring Out Old Friendship

He replied with a smile, not caring much: "If one person sues me, I am the defendant. If a group of people sues me, I am just a defendant. Conversely, if I am one person and everyone thinks it's a very serious women's issue, and I sue a group of people, it's just a women's issue. I've figured it out this way, so what am I afraid of?" He became excited, disregarding everything, and continued to express his grievances. The interviewer saw that he was speaking without any restraint and that it was public, so he marked the most important words in his notebook, secretly recording them. Jia Duocai clearly saw this but smiled at him: "Brother, this is just private talk, treating you as a friend, that's why I spoke so casually. I think you understand this in your heart and wouldn't publish these words in the newspaper." The interviewer smiled: "I don't think there's any harm in that. Anyway, Mr. Jia is prepared to sue them, so why be afraid of offending them? Moreover, Mr. Jia is a person of status and wouldn't go back on his words, right?" As he spoke, he closed his notebook and put it in his pocket. Then, he stood up to take his leave. Jia Duocai was very distressed, not being able to stop him and not being able to let him go. So, he smiled and rushed to the door, saying: "I still have a lot to talk about with you. As a news reporter, although the more news material, the better, you should also know the art of capturing and releasing the interviewee." The interviewer smiled: "I am very happy for Mr. Jia to tell me more. However, my working hours have arrived, and I don't have time to write it down. I think Mr. Jia would allow me to publish all the conversations in the newspaper, and we would be very grateful." As he spoke, he turned his body sideways, squeezed out of the door, and smiled, nodding and saying: "Goodbye, goodbye." Before Jia Duocai could say anything, he had already walked far away. Jia Duocai stood at the door, lost in thought. He had been too excited just now and gave the reporter a lot of material. When it is published tomorrow, these ladies will definitely react strongly. This Little West Heaven is their base camp, and perhaps tomorrow they will repeat today's scene. (892)

Love Duel at the Foot of Mount Kiso in Japan

— Yan

Mount Kiso is the only mountain in Japan with many pines and cypresses, and several thousand families live nearby. Their occupations can be roughly divided into four types: one is agriculture, in addition to planting grains and mulberry trees, they also plant various fruits and operate simple pottery businesses; one is fishing, there are many natural rivers near the mountain for them to fish in, but recently most people dig ponds to raise fish and make canned foods to be transported to the city; one is handicraft industry, which is carving various shells into simple and rough works of art; and one is commerce, transporting products from the villages of Kiso to various places, and at the same time transporting the things needed by the mountain people. Among these four occupations, commerce is the easiest, and the people who work in handicrafts live well, and they mostly live at the foot of Mount Kiso.

The various houses at the foot of Mount Kiso have a different kind of beautiful scenery because of the pines and cypresses interspersed between them. Often, a shell carving is hung in front of each household, and red silk and green ribbons flutter in the wind with this artwork, which is very beautiful. Moreover, many households tie a small bell to the silk thread or ribbon, and the bell also makes a sound, which is particularly lively, and they sing songs to each other, which is tireless all day long. During festivals, especially the New Year, everyone wears new clothes and holds many art objects, either throwing them as ball games or wearing them as decorations, as if they have not yet broken away from the barbaric era, and they dance in various ways in the shade of the pine and cypress trees. When they dance, they always take shell carvings as dancing objects, and the dancing postures are very strange. The four words "more jumping than dancing" can really describe most of their postures.

Although their dances are mixed with men and women, there is also a very strict boundary. This boundary is different from other parts of Japan, that is, unmarried men and women can absolutely not dance with each other except with their parents. Therefore, the young men and women who dance must be married couples, otherwise, once it is found out, the parents will consider it the greatest shame and often send their children to monasteries or nunneries, and at the same time, they will never dance with each other again to avoid mentioning their feelings. It is said that in a certain village at the foot of this mountain in the past, there was a rich man whose unmarried daughter actually danced privately with an unknown unmarried man. Later, the rich man found out and poisoned his daughter to death, and he himself cut his hair and became a monk, holding a pessimistic view of everything in the world. This custom is extremely strange. At the same time, there is also a strange custom of love duels, which is not found in other parts of Japan, but is still prevailing in the foothills.

Love duels are held every year on the 15th of January, the 15th of July, and the 15th of October under the supervision of the village chief. The reason for holding them is often that two or three men fall in love with one woman, resulting in the woman's parents being unable to make a decision, or the woman's parents do not allow the man she likes, or the woman does not want to marry the man her parents like. After a love duel, the village chief judges who can be elected as the woman's husband, then the men and women all express their obedience.

The place for love duels is in a large open space at the foot of the mountain. On the day of the duel, all the people in the village come to watch. The men who duel all wear black hats and hold shell weapons in their hands to fight each other. After fifteen minutes of fighting, the village chief determines who wins and who loses. The victorious man is lifted up by many relatives, shouting victory, while the loser hangs his head and goes home with his relatives, who are all silent.

On the morning of the duel, the woman who is the object of the duel makes herself up very beautifully because that day is no different from her engagement day. However, she does not go out, but waits at home. As soon as the duel is over, she and her parents go out to dance, expressing their congratulations, but they must not dance with the victor of the duel before the formal marriage.

Sky Burial and Cremation

— Lu Hua

Sky burial is a custom that still exists in Tibet. That is, after a person dies, regardless of gender or age, the flesh is cut off piece by piece, and then the bones are smashed with a large iron cone to feed the birds and beasts, which is called sky burial. This method of cutting the flesh and the strange phenomenon of vultures vying for food were actually filmed by the photography team brought by Envoy Huang Musong when he went to Tibet last year. This newsreel has been shown once by the Moonlight Film Company. I was also in attendance. Seeing this torture that involved both dismemberment and bone crushing, one cannot help but feel a different kind of unbearable feeling! But in the Tibetan sense, it is believed that only in this way can the sins of the deceased be eliminated during his lifetime, and it is believed that the soul can ascend to heaven only if its corpse is completely eaten by birds and beasts.

Because I mentioned sky burial in Tibet, I also thought of a strange custom of cremation that is practiced among the southwestern barbarians. Cremation is a funeral method of a tribe of barbarians in the northwestern border of He County, Yunnan Province. When a person dies in their family, it is customary not to mourn, and they do not use a coffin. They only use a carrying pole through the body and carry it to the wilderness, where they pile up dead trees and burn it. This is called cremation. Only when the corpse is burned into charcoal do everyone cry loudly to show their grief. However, during the cremation, the people present must raise their hands and jump, shout wildly, and at the same time take wooden clappers, bamboo tubes, or copper and iron響器 to beat frantically, drumming and making a lot of noise, making a mess. It is said that the reason they make such a noise is to scare away the birds in the sky, so as not to come down and抢食 the meat of the dead. Because they believe that if the meat of the dead is eaten by birds, its soul will not ascend to heaven.

Batak Marriage Customs

— Green Moss

In the Dutch East Indies, Sumatra, there is a native people called the Batak. Due to their geographic location, they mature very early physically. Both boys and girls reach marriageable age at thirteen. For girls, it can be delayed by a year or two, which isn't a big deal, but for boys, marriage at thirteen is a must. Overseas Chinese children there who haven't married by seventeen or eighteen are considered quite strange.

Batak houses have two levels: people live upstairs, and pigs, cows, and other livestock are kept downstairs. However, when a boy turns thirteen, his family no longer allows him to live upstairs; he must sleep with the pigs and cows until he finds a spouse, after which he is allowed to live upstairs.

The Batak people have very immature knowledge and no sense of etiquette. The relationship between men and women is very casual. As long as a woman consents, there are no issues with sexual intercourse. Married women add a white border to their blue hats; unmarried women only wear blue hats. Any Batak man can flirt with any woman, but married women are less willing. They are very happy to flirt with unmarried women, and they will grant any request. After a Batak man meets an unfamiliar woman, he can ask, "Can I go play with you?" or "Shall we eat together?" If the woman agrees, you can go to the woods with her and do whatever you want.

The Batak people practice polygamy; a man can marry as many wives as he pleases. Batak women are very good at production work, endure hardship, and accumulate a lot of wealth to provide for their husbands to squander. The current Batak chieftain has over thirty wives.

Another strange thing about the Batak people is that it's hard to distinguish fathers from sons, because after a Batak father dies, his son has an obligation to marry his mother or his father's concubine. If a woman becomes pregnant and her husband dies, the child born is considered the inherited son, but in reality, he is his younger brother. The Batak people don't think about this.

The article focuses on health and wellness, and it is essential reading for both old and young, male and female. Send 5 jiao to No. 14, Lane 24, Tongfu Road, Shanghai, to subscribe for the whole year and receive two free copies. We are pleased to introduce it.
